On the treatment of scarring on the upper eyelid.
Axcirnath is a serious condition that develops in the layers of skin on the eyelid, especially in children. It worsens their vision and affects their cataract development; they cannot bear to look at the brightness of the sun as it causes them to tear up excessively.
So you see them constantly rubbing their faces and eyelids while sleeping; the skin above their eyelashes is moist, already covered in inflammation, with an apparent threat of infection present in the eye; and when you press that area with your fingers, you feel a lump under it.
One method of operation is as follows: the patient places their head on your lap, and you cover them with a cloth, making sure it's loose; then stretch the skin around the lump according to how big the swelling is, place that over the bump, and press all sides with your fingers so the lump moves towards the middle; finally make an incision at the center of that area with a spatula, but be careful not to make the slit any bigger than what's necessary for flaubotomia.
Make sure you remove the entire cyst before closing the wound, because in most cases pus forms under the skin and spreads through an incision in the shape of white streaks.

And there are some who sprinkle salt, placing it in the cavity of the incision to absorb any moisture that remains.
Then care for them until they heal completely.
If the wound becomes infected with abscesses, treat them with soft poultices of cedar until they are healed.

Of the cure for inflammation of the eyelid which is done below.
This inflammation of the eyelid, which is truly called alxacrati; and it can be either natural or accidental.
Accidental inflammation is caused by trauma, incision, cauterization, or other similar injuries.
The method of operation is as follows: take a needle with double thread and insert it into the flesh, passing from the left tear duct to the right one, ensuring that the thread reaches both ends of the flesh.
Then stretch the flesh away from the divided parts using the needle and sew it with the needle, making an incision with a broad spatula. And so restore the shape of the eyelid as needed; if not, take a strip and place it over the divided form, and with this reshape the eyelid, closing both fissures on the side of the lower eyelid.
And if the ends of both fissures are at two corners of the incision which you have made so that they meet, and from these is formed an angle when brought together to form a shape.

And then remove that flesh in an amount equal to his thumb's width under him; this is the same size as the eyelid.
Then adjust the separated parts and sew them together with woolen thread; afterward, treat them with the softening medicines and poultices we have discussed until they are healed.
If any harshness occurs due to a crack or suture or cauterization, then it is necessary to make a flat incision over the skin of the eyelid as previously described. Then separate the poultice between the two lips, as we have mentioned earlier.
In the conclusion of this treatise on treating harshness when it is excessive or insufficient, let it be remembered during the operation that its preparation for treatment takes various forms.
A skilled practitioner should always prepare an invention in any way possible to make the patient's figure return to its natural form or close to it, and this harshness according to what is suitable for the operation and instruments with the best arrangements.

On curing baldness."
This ailment that is called *alconati* is nothing but a discharge, which is adjusted in the hole resembling water flowing downwards and it is not that.
Now the way to proceed with this treatment is as follows: place the patient on a prepared and straight saddle-shaped cushion, then take his head in your two hands and direct it so that you can see where the health originates from within him, and ensure it remains dry and does not descend, block out all light so he cannot see, and let the patient be aware of what is being done.
And if it does not flow downwards, then you know this is water (humidity) at work.
But if the path for health to descend is not prepared as we have described, then let the patient lie between your two hands and take a fine spatula and apply it over the panniculus carnosus near where the conjunctiva continues onto the cornea in the eye (at the white part), so that health may be expelled.
So once it is expelled, then you must distill into the affected area a warm water infusion in which you have mixed honey or an infusion of boiled fenugreek and honey.
Then treat with other remedies as necessary until the patient is cured.

Regarding the treatment of raw flesh within the nasal cavity:
When various pieces of raw flesh grow inside the nose, causing blockages that resemble either a scorpion's stinger or a sea polyp, this condition is known as 'polypus' because it takes on the form of said polyp. And there is flesh that is cancerous, ulcerated, and of a dark color; it is not the healthy flesh of a lion but rather discolored.
So when the patient has healthy flesh that is not fraudulent or cancerous, let them sit between your legs and expose their body to the sun. Open up their nostrils and prick the affected flesh with a lancet. Then extract that which has been separated outside, and carefully cut away what you have understood to be affected by the sharp, thin knife from one side until you know all the flesh has been opened; if there remains any cause for which excision is possible, then take it out with one of your fine instruments while making sure no causes remain. But if you see blood flowing or an evil abscess appear, then apply what is needed; should it be one of the malignant abscesses, then incise and cauterize that area while making sure the blood flows out and all cavities are opened.

Title: Chapter 40.
In which is the summary of the sermon regarding appreciation of abscesses and the sectioning of them.
Abscesses are special marks, of many shapes, according to their recollection, each described in this book.
And they are diverse in their perforation and sectioning due to two methods: one is specific to the type of abscess itself; and another considers what it has absorbed from moistures.
The second method is based on the locations where accidents occur in the body, as an abscess on the head differs from that on the buttocks; an abscess on a fleshy area varies from one at a joint; and each requires its own judgment for operation.
Most abscesses should not be perforated but instead allowed to mature or heal on their own.
Other abscesses should be pierced when they are hard and do not mature according to their fullness; this includes abscesses near joints, as an abscess by a joint prolongs the healing process until you can treat its cause, which is often corruption of the ligaments or nerves of that joint, leading to contraction of that limb; or it is close to a principal member, and delaying perforation while awaiting maturation may damage the principal member; or it is near the buttocks, so pierce this one before it matures; do not pierce harshly when digestion is incomplete, but rather wait for one near the buttocks, so you do not harm the perineum and prolong healing of the interior parts of the buttocks, resulting in a fistula, or that it be done in its term without being cured. Mays cove que tu sapias la hora de la perforacio de la apostema, e aysso es quan es maturat.

On the treatment of intestinal hernia.
This hernia's occurrence is due to an incision that originates in the diaphragm extended over the abdomen from parts of the abdominal muscles, so that when these are ruptured some intestines will exit through this rupture.
This rupture is either of the hip joint or the thigh bone and this type can occur for several reasons: through a blow, or due to a fall, or by lifting something heavy, or similar actions.
The sign of this [condition], when it is due to an extended hip joint injury, shows up gradually over time and not suddenly; the reason being that pus has formed between the bone and where the hip joint presses against the intestine.
The sign of this [condition] is when it is caused by an injury to the thigh bone; at first there will be intense pain that suddenly strikes and there will also appear swelling below the injured area itself, with pus forming where the intestine has been pierced or the body has been torn open around the hip joint.
Sometimes you have to put the intestine back in its place through an opening made by the hernia; this type of hernia is called inguinal [hernia].
Sometimes air is trapped in the abdomen and sometimes a hole appears in the intestine where air gets stuck; this can greatly harm the patient who may suffer severe pain when pressed upon there.
And in the treatment of this specific type of illness with iron instruments, there is fear involved; hence it should be avoided during menstruation.
The method of operation for this condition is as follows: instruct the patient to push the intestine back into its cavity using their hand if it has returned; then place them on their side with their legs elevated.
Then grasp the cord that connects to the testes at its origin, make an incision along the entire length of the cord, and insert two hooks into the edges of the incision as needed to open it with those.

Now insert your finger into the opening that is below the testes, within the white capsule, which is located beneath the cord of the patient; and remove any adhesions found near the back of the testis.

De extraccio de sagetas translates to "On arrow extraction.
Sagetas (arrows) are diverse depending on the species and the parts of the body they target, as their diversity consists of those with large points, small ones, concave tips, blunt ends, solid bodies; and those with three edges, some with tongues, and others with barbs.
The signs of the brain being struck by an arrow are: if it pierces through bone and comes out from above, causing intense headaches, blindness, vertigo, ringing in the ears, inflammation, and redness on the tongue, spasms, mixed-up reasoning, vomiting bile, having a hard time speaking, losing their voice. White discharge resembling dust emerges from around the wound, along with watery fluids coming from the flesh itself.
And so if these signs appear to you, then refrain from the cure and extraction of the arrow unless it is necessary.
But the signs of an arrow in the heart are when it is close to the left nipple, and you feel that it has lodged in hard tissue, not soft; and also if the movement of the arrow resembles the pulse, and black blood flows out, with coldness in the extremities, a weak pulse, and fainting; and so you should know that death descends swiftly soon after.
And the signs when an arrow has pierced the lung are a great outflow of frothy blood, and the vessels near the neck become inflamed, the patient's complexion changes, they exhale heavily, and crave cold air.
If the arrow grazes the membrane that is near the foot, and the pain is close to the little toes, it causes a great swelling with intense pain and sighing, but not all of the muscles in the limbs are affected.
And if an arrow strikes the stomach, then often some undigested food will be vomited.
And if the arrow is lodged in the abdomen and cannot be removed through incision or by drawing it out with a ligature (i.e., by pulling on it), then make an opening into the wound, or the hernia or intestine that has been ruptured so that there is no hope of extracting the arrow.
And if the arrow penetrates into and perforates the bladder causing urine to be discharged through it (the wound) or some other part of the body exterior to the bladder, and possibly there is pain in the patient, then know that this situation is fatal.
All other body parts such as the face, neck, throat, shoulders, vertebrae of the back, breast bone, hip, leg and similar limbs are salvageable according to medical experts' opinions if the arrow does not penetrate a vein or artery nor is it poison-tipped.
And I recount this to you regarding what I know about the nature of these arrows so that you can understand their treatment.
The reason is this: once I extracted an arrow from one man's eye socket at the root of his nose and created a new opening behind his ear; he was healed without further injury to the eye.

Chapter 2: On fractures that occur in the head.
The types of fractures are many, and their forms are diverse, with distinct causes. Some fractures occur due to the impact of space, where the impact drives all bone matter into the hollow at one end, similar to what occurs in wood; this type is known as axial fracture. Or the space cuts through a part of the bone, dividing it from its flesh without piercing completely through; such fractures are called absolute levations.
The extent of damage in these two types of fractures can be severe or minor, and the third type is either an open or closed fracture; this results from impact with a blunt object or striking against stone, akin to each other.
And this fracture is penetrating close to the bone marrow, which lies beneath the bone; or it is on the surface of the bone, and the wound caused by these two types of fractures can be large or small.

On the treatment for dislocation of the hip.
Be aware that the hip joint is dislocated with difficulty and returns with difficulty; it can be dislocated in all directions but mostly to the front of the back part, and its dislocation cannot be hidden from you when it sags under your gaze or touch regardless of how it's dislocated. And when you realign the dislocated hip with your hand, this is made clear to you because the joint is concave and unable to bend the arm or reach with its muscle.

Sometimes the shoulder joint of the hand is dislocated, and its reduction can be gentle; it is different for other joints. However, speed in reducing it when it is dislocated is necessary before the area becomes inflamed or infected.

Of the treatment for dislocation of the vertebrae in the spine.
When there is an accident causing complete dislocation of one or more vertebrae in the spine or neck, and these are significantly displaced from their original positions, there is no cure because death ensues for the patient.
The sign of this is that the patient's excretion happens involuntarily and they cannot control it; often, some body parts become soft or two of their legs or arms, or one of those; or a vertebra is dislocated from its position as many times it is dislocated in four directions.
So when the vertebra has been displaced backward, this is called 'hernia'.
However, the treatment of this condition is that one must first consider whether the hernia occurred during childhood because in such cases there is neither a cure nor complete healing.
But in cases that arise from crushing or beating or similar incidents, the Ancients have described various methods of treatment which I will discuss at length later since they are very beneficial; but here I shall briefly summarize them due to my proximity and understanding of these matters so as not to be too wordy. I have set out this treatise with diverse instruments that illustrate what has been discussed.
And only that swelling which occurs directly on the back is cured by what I recommend.
And if the patient is extended on their back near a wall, and they are covered with wet sheets to prevent their feet from being visible.
Then a straight stick should be placed and fixed into the ground at the head end of the patient's body, with another stick around their feet at the other end.
The minister should hold the stick, and they must not be standing in a pit or trench; another minister should hold the other stick accordingly.
Then wrap a thin thread around the patient's head and leave it loose; extend the end of this thread to the stick that is near their head, and tie it there; then tighten the other thread over their hips and behind them, extending down towards their legs; finally, tighten all the threads and secure them together on the other stick which is by their feet.

Chapter 31.
For treating a dislocated hip.
Know that the hip joint and muscle junction can only be injured by dislocation, and it is not affected like other joints with small displacements or concavities.
The hip joint can be dislocated in four ways: either internally or externally, anteriorly or posteriorly.
It is mostly dislocated internally, and rarely anteriorly or posteriorly.
The sign of internal dislocation is when you align the patient's affected leg with the healthy one, it appears longer and the knee more prominent than on the healthy side; the patient cannot bend their foot inwards and the area around the ankle becomes swollen and tender to touch due to an accumulation of pus beneath the skin because the head of the thigh bone has reached this point.
The sign of external dislocation is the opposite of internal: when you align the patient's affected leg with the healthy one, it appears shorter and the knee less prominent than on the healthy side; the patient can bend their foot outwards but cannot bend it inwards, and there is no swelling or tenderness around the ankle.

And the sign of dislocation is when you command the patient to bring their leg towards the hip; then, you will know that the joint is indeed dislocated.
The restoration process for all types of dislocations is as follows: make the patient lie straight and have them extend their leg if possible; place your face against theirs, with both your hands on their cheeks, then put their foot between your feet; grasp their affected joint with your palms firmly, keeping it there with a grip that rests upon your knuckles until another helper extends their leg to allow for the joint's return to its proper position.
The sign of successful relocation is when the patient's leg naturally adheres to their hip without any forced effort.
Then, plaster that area and keep the leg attached to the hip with bindings for three or four days; afterward, untie those bandages.
Do not let the patient walk for a few days until they are fully healed and comfortable.
But if you have mistakenly failed to reduce the dislocation and thus caused damage by applying force, administer gentle extensions with the aid of soft cloths during its treatment as previously described for hip injuries.
Chapter 33.
Of the cure for the dislocation of the ankle.
Sometimes the ankle is sprained due to slight displacement, and sometimes it is dislocated according to its severity. The dislocation can occur either on the inside or outside of the joint.
The sign of an ankle dislocation is that you will see swelling in the direction where it has been displaced.
In the case of a sprain, the cure is usually simple and involves gentle stretching with the hands until it pops back into place.
When treating a severe dislocation, it is necessary to make the patient lie down straight and have a strong and brave assistant stand behind their back at their mid-point.
Then you will place your right hand on the upper part of their foot and your left hand at the lower part of their foot in the area of the ankle.
Then pull the foot towards you with your right hand and do so twice with your left hand. Afterwards, extend your left hand, using the toes of the foot to push down against the shin without effort.
And repeat this procedure twice according to our count.
Then wrap the foot around the leg for the third time, and you are at the ankle.
So if you return once or twice in this manner and see the foot swelling, it is good; otherwise, repeat the operation as the swelling persists.
However, if it is forbidden for you to perform the reduction as we have described, then make the patient lie on their back on the ground, and place a very thick pillow under them, between their thighs, and wrap them in cloth so that they do not catch cold.
Then the minister of him holds their thighs, and another minister stretches out the foot with his hands or with a cloth that is tied around the ankle; then each minister extends against the extension of their own side, and the pillow remains between the patient's thighs to prevent their body from being pulled apart due to this extension.
Then the doctor grasps the dislocation with his hands and another minister holds the healthy thigh apart, as the dislocation easily returns to its place.

On treating the dislocation of the aforementioned bones in the feet.
Cove que aquel qu’es dislocat sia engualhat am pauca extencio ses trebal; e aquo que no es dificil, abantz es leugier.
If the dislocation is in any of the joints of the foot, then you must make the patient place their foot on a level surface on the ground or on a table, and they should remain standing like that as if walking.
Then stand on your feet and place your foot over what protrudes from the joints; then step on it with your foot firmly until it returns to its original position, and you see that it is level again without any prominence.
Then place under the patient's belly of their foot a table that supports the entire foot, which has two ends; then bind it with a decent and firm bandage for three days. Then untie it and make them rest from walking for many days until they are strengthened and assured of recovery.

Regarding the types of dislocation caused by blow, fracture, or any other accident.
When any of these causes happen and you engage in the treatment and restoration of them, many times death occurs.
And for this reason, it is not appropriate to boast about the patient's recovery; instead, one should be humble and leave judgment to the divine. One must use mild medicines at first that only cause small abscesses, allowing the illness to run its natural course unless a cure or relief from suffering is expected, in which case hope appears. Therefore, strive to make the reduction of their condition as soon as possible at its initial stage, before it develops into a severe abscess.
And if the limb returns to its desired position, then apply a treatment that encourages mild abscesses and cures the sore with a suitable drying ointment.
If dislocation is accompanied by a fracture and the bones are separated, you must pierce their membrane and treat them as we have previously discussed for simple illnesses in such cases.
Beware and avoid according to your virtue any instrument that causes harm in the ways of fear, as my previous teachings have instructed you; for this is better for your true Creator, more permanent for your glory, and more wholesome for your true body in its time.
